<p><b>Guinea-Bissau</b>, officially the <b>Republic of Guinea-Bissau</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; padding: 0 .1em;" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg" title="File:En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'g' in 'guy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɡ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɪ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">i</span></a></span> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɪ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">s</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/aʊ/ 'ou' in 'pout'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">aʊ</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>, <span title="English pronunciation respelling" class="Unicode"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Wikipedia:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">GI</span></span></span></b>-nee-bi-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">SOW</span></span></span></b></i></a></span>, (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>República da Guiné-Bissau</i></span>, <small>pronounced:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese_and_Galician" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese and Galician">[ʁeˈpublikɐ dɐ ɡiˈnɛ biˈsaw]</a></span>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. It covers 36,125&#160;km² (nearly 14,000 sq mi) with an estimated population of 1,704,000.</p>
<p>Guinea-Bissau was once part of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kaabu" title="Kaabu">Gabu</a>, as well as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>. Parts of this kingdom persisted until the 18th century, while a few others were under some rule by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> since the 16th century. In the 19th century, it was colonized as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>. Upon independence, declared in 1973 and recognised in 1974, the name of its capital, <a href="/wiki/Bissau" title="Bissau">Bissau</a>, was added to the country's name to prevent confusion with Guinea (formerly <a href="/wiki/French_Guinea" title="French Guinea">French Guinea</a>). Guinea-Bissau has a history of political instability since independence, and no elected president has successfully served a full five-year term.</p>
<p>On the evening of 12 April 2012, members of the country's military staged a <a href="/wiki/2012_Guinea-Bissau_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Guinea-Bissau coup d'état">coup d'état</a> and arrested the interim president and a leading presidential candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Former vice chief of staff, General <a href="/wiki/Mamadu_Ture_Kuruma" title="Mamadu Ture Kuruma">Mamadu Ture Kuruma</a>, assumed control of the country in the transitional period and started negotiations with opposition parties.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Only 14% of the population speaks <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, established as the official language in the colonial period. Almost half the population (44%) speaks <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole" class="mw-redirect">Crioulo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">Portuguese-based creole language</a>, and the remainder speak a variety of native African languages. The main religions are <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religions" title="African traditional religions" class="mw-redirect">African traditional religions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>; there is a <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (mostly Roman Catholic) minority. The country's per-capita <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">lowest in the world</a>.</p>
<p>Guinea-Bissau is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" title="La Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">La Francophonie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="History of Guinea-Bissau">History of Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a></div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau was once part of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kaabu" title="Kaabu">Gabu</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>; parts of this kingdom persisted until the 18th century. Other parts of the territory in the current country were considered by the Portuguese as part of their <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a> was known as the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast" title="Slave Coast">Slave Coast</a>, as it was a major area for the exportation of African slaves by Europeans to the western hemisphere. Previously slaves had been traded by Arabs north to the northern part of Africa and into the Middle East.</p>
<p>Early reports of Europeans reaching this area include those of the <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venetian</a> <a href="/wiki/Alvise_Cadamosto" title="Alvise Cadamosto">Alvise Cadamosto</a>'s voyage of 1455,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> the 1479–1480 voyage by Flemish-French trader <a href="/wiki/Eustache_de_la_Fosse" title="Eustache de la Fosse">Eustache de la Fosse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo Cão">Diogo Cão</a>. In the 1480s this Portuguese explorer reached the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and the lands of <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo" class="mw-redirect">Bakongo</a>, setting up the foundations of modern <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, some 4200&#160;km down the African coast from Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although the rivers and coast of this area were among the first places colonized by the Portuguese, who set up trading posts in the 16th century, they did not explore the interior until the 19th century. The local African rulers in Guinea, some of whom prospered greatly from the <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade" class="mw-redirect">slave trade</a>, controlled the inland trade and did not allow the Europeans into the interior. They kept them in the fortified coastal settlements where the trading took place.<sup id="cite_ref-history_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> African communities that fought back against slave traders also distrusted European adventurers and would-be settlers. The Portuguese in Guinea were largely restricted to the port of <a href="/wiki/Bissau" title="Bissau">Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cacheu" title="Cacheu">Cacheu</a>. A small number of European settlers established isolated farms along Bissau's inland rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-history_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For a brief period in the 1790s, the British tried to establish a rival foothold on an offshore island, at <a href="/wiki/Bolama" title="Bolama">Bolama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> But by the 19th century the Portuguese were sufficiently secure in Bissau to regard the neighbouring coastline as their own special territory, also up north in part of present South Senegal.</p>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_War_of_Independence" title="Guinea-Bissau War of Independence">armed rebellion</a> beginning in 1956 by the <a href="/wiki/Partido_Africano_da_Independ%C3%AAncia_da_Guin%C3%A9_e_Cabo_Verde" title="Partido Africano da Independência da Guiné e Cabo Verde" class="mw-redirect">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a> (PAIGC) under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Amílcar Cabral">Amílcar Cabral</a> gradually consolidated its hold on then <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike guerrilla movements in other <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonies</a>, the PAIGC rapidly extended its military control over large portions of the territory, aided by the jungle-like terrain, its easily reached borderlines with neighbouring allies, and large quantities of arms from <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and left-leaning African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Cuba also agreed to supply artillery experts, doctors, and technicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Cuba.21_Africa.21_Revolution.21_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cuba.21_Africa.21_Revolution.21-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The PAIGC even managed to acquire a significant anti-aircraft capability in order to defend itself against aerial attack. By 1973, the PAIGC was in control of many parts of Guinea, although the movement suffered a setback in January 1973 when Cabral was assassinated.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281973.29">Independence (1973)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Independence (1973)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/250px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" width="250" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/375px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/500px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2381" data-file-height="2149" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/PAIGC" title="PAIGC" class="mw-redirect">PAIGC</a> forces raise the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Flag of Guinea-Bissau">flag of Guinea-Bissau</a> in 1974.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Independence was unilaterally declared on 24 September 1973. Recognition became universal following 25 April 1974 socialist-inspired <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">military coup</a> in Portugal, which overthrew Lisbon's <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Cabral" title="Luís Cabral">Luís Cabral</a>, brother of Amílcar and co-founder of PAIGC, was appointed the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="President of Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect">President of Guinea-Bissau</a>. Following independence, the PAIGC killed thousands of local Guinean soldiers who had fought along with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army" title="Portuguese Army">Portuguese Army</a> against guerrillas. Some escaped to settle in Portugal or other African nations.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> One of the massacres occurred in the town of <a href="/wiki/Bissor%C3%A3" title="Bissorã">Bissorã</a>. In 1980 the PAIGC acknowledged in its newspaper <i>Nó Pintcha</i> (dated 29 November 1980) that many Gueinean soldiers had been executed and buried in unmarked collective graves in the woods of Cumerá, Portogole, and Mansabá.</p>
<p>The country was controlled by a revolutionary council until 1984. The first multi-party elections were held in 1994. An army uprising in May 1998 led to the <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Civil_War" title="Guinea-Bissau Civil War">Guinea-Bissau Civil War</a> and the president's ousting in June 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Elections were held again in 2000, and <a href="/wiki/Kumba_Ial%C3%A1" title="Kumba Ialá">Kumba Ialá</a> was elected president.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2003, a military coup was conducted. The military arrested Ialá on the charge of being "unable to solve the problems".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> After being delayed several times, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_legislative_election,_2004" title="Guinea-Bissau legislative election, 2004">legislative elections</a> were held in March 2004. A <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutiny</a> of military factions in October 2004 resulted in the death of the head of the armed forces and caused widespread unrest.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vieira_years">Vieira years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Vieira years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG/300px-Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG/450px-Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG/600px-Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bissau_-_Abandoned_tank.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Abandoned tank from the <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Civil_War" title="Guinea-Bissau Civil War">1998–1999 civil war</a> in the capital Bissau, 2003.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 2005, presidential elections were held for the first time since the coup that deposed Ialá. Ialá returned as the candidate for the PRS, claiming to be the legitimate president of the country, but the election was won by former president <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Bernardo_Vieira" title="João Bernardo Vieira">João Bernardo Vieira</a>, deposed in the 1999 coup. Vieira beat <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a> in a runoff election. Sanhá initially refused to concede, claiming that <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">tampering</a> and electoral fraud occurred in two <a href="/wiki/Constituencies" title="Constituencies" class="mw-redirect">constituencies</a> including the capital, Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite reports of arms entering the country prior to the election and some "disturbances during campaigning," including attacks on government offices by unidentified gunmen, foreign <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">election monitors</a> described the 2005 election overall as "calm and organized".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Three years later, PAIGC won a strong parliamentary majority, with 67 of 100 seats, in the parliamentary election held in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2008, President Vieira's official residence was attacked by members of the armed forces, killing a guard but leaving the president unharmed.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 March 2009, however, Vieira was assassinated by what preliminary reports indicated to be a group of soldiers avenging the death of the head of joint chiefs of staff, General <a href="/wiki/Batista_Tagme_Na_Wai" title="Batista Tagme Na Wai" class="mw-redirect">Batista Tagme Na Wai</a>. Tagme died in an explosion on Sunday, 1 March 2009, target of an assassination. Military leaders in the country pledged to respect the constitutional order of succession. National Assembly Speaker <a href="/wiki/Raimundo_Pereira" title="Raimundo Pereira">Raimundo Pereira</a> was appointed as an interim president until a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_presidential_election,_2009" title="Guinea-Bissau presidential election, 2009">election</a> on 28 June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> It was won by <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Politics of Guinea-Bissau">Politics of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bissau3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bissau3.jpg/300px-Bissau3.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bissau3.jpg/450px-Bissau3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bissau3.jpg/600px-Bissau3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bissau3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Assembly_(Guinea-Bissau)" title="National People's Assembly (Guinea-Bissau)">National People's Assembly of Guinea-Bissau</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau is a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. In the past, the government had been highly centralized. Multi-party governance was not established until mid-1991. The president is the head of state and the prime minister is the head of government. Since 1974, no president has successfully served a full five year term.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the legislative level, a unicameral <i>Assembleia Nacional Popular</i> (<a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Assembly_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="National People's Assembly of Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect">National People's Assembly</a>) is made up of 100 members. They are popularly elected from multi-member constituencies to serve a four-year term. The judicial system is headed by a <i>Tribunal Supremo da Justiça</i> (Supreme Court), made up of nine justices appointed by the president; they serve at the pleasure of the president.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Bernardo_Vieira" title="João Bernardo Vieira">João Bernardo "Nino" Vieira</a> was elected in 2005 as President of Guinea-Bissau as an independent, being declared winner of the second round by the CNE (Comité Nacional de Eleições). Vieira returned to power in 2005 six years after being ousted from office during a civil war. Previously, he held power for 19 years after taking power in 1980 in a <a href="/wiki/Bloodless_coup" title="Bloodless coup" class="mw-redirect">bloodless coup</a>. In that action, he toppled the government of Luís Cabral.</p>
<p>He was killed on 2 March 2009, possibly by soldiers in retaliation for the assassination of General <a href="/wiki/Batista_Tagme_Na_Waie" title="Batista Tagme Na Waie">Batista Tagme Na Waie</a>, the head of the joint chiefs of staff, killed in an explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Vieira's death did not trigger widespread violence, but there were signs of turmoil in the country, according to the <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">advocacy group</a> <a href="/wiki/Swisspeace" title="Swisspeace">Swisspeace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a> was elected after a transition. In the 2009 election to replace the assassinated Vieira, Sanhá was the presidential candidate of the PAIGC while <a href="/wiki/Kumba_Ial%C3%A1" title="Kumba Ialá">Kumba Ialá</a> was the presidential candidate of the PRS.</p>
<p>In 2012, President Rachide Sambu-balde <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a> died. He belonged to PAIGC (<a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Guinea_and_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a>), one of the two major political parties in Guinea-Bissau, along with the PRS (<a href="/wiki/Party_for_Social_Renewal" title="Party for Social Renewal">Party for Social Renewal</a>). There are more than 20 minor parties.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Foreign relations of Guinea-Bissau">Foreign relations of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau follows a nonaligned foreign policy and seeks friendly and cooperative relations with a wide variety of states and organizations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Military of Guinea-Bissau">Military of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>A 2008 estimate put the size of the Guinea-Bissau Armed Forces at around 4,000 personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Regions of Guinea-Bissau">Regions of Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">Sectors of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="floatright">

</div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau is divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Regions of Guinea-Bissau">regions</a> (<span lang="pt"><i>regiões</i></span>) and one <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" title="Autonomous entity" class="mw-redirect">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">sector</a> (<span lang="pt"><i>sector autónomo</i></span>). These, in turn, are subdivided into 37 <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">Sectors</a>. The regions are:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Geography of Guinea-Bissau">Geography of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-guinea-bissau.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Un-guinea-bissau.png/450px-Un-guinea-bissau.png" width="450" height="344" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Un-guinea-bissau.png/675px-Un-guinea-bissau.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Un-guinea-bissau.png/900px-Un-guinea-bissau.png 2x" data-file-width="2709" data-file-height="2073" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-guinea-bissau.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of Guinea Bissau.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20130612-DSC_9042_(9290793821)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-20130612-DSC_9042_%289290793821%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4799" data-file-height="3179" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20130612-DSC_9042_(9290793821)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bissau-Guinean landscape.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20130611-DSC_9018_(9290631541)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/230px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg" width="230" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/345px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/460px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20130611-DSC_9018_(9290631541)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typical scenery in Guinea-Bissau.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to the south and east, with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to its west. Guinea-Bissau lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_parallel_north" title="11th parallel north">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a> (a small area is south of 11°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/13th_meridian_west" title="13th meridian west">13°</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_meridian_west" title="17th meridian west">17°W</a>.</p>
<p>At 36,125 square kilometres (13,948&#160;sq&#160;mi), the country is larger in size than <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. Guinea-Bissau lies at a low altitude; its highest point is 300 metres (984&#160;ft). The terrain of Guinea-Bissau is mostly low coastal plain with swamps of <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a> rising to <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-fact_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fact-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-like rainy season alternates with periods of hot, dry <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> winds blowing from the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bijagos_Archipelago" title="Bijagos Archipelago" class="mw-redirect">Bijagos Archipelago</a> lies off of the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Climate of Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect">Climate of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau is warm all year around and there is little temperature fluctuation; it averages 26.3&#160;°C (79.3&#160;°F). The average rainfall for Bissau is 2,024 millimetres (79.7&#160;in) although this is almost entirely accounted for during the rainy season which falls between June and September/October. From December through April, the country experiences drought.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png" class="image"><img alt="Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png/600px-Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png" width="600" height="416" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png/900px-Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Klimadiagramm-deutsch-Bissau-Guinea-Bissau.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="710" /></a></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Severe environmental issues include <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>; soil erosion; overgrazing and overfishing.<sup id="cite_ref-fact_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fact-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Economy of Guinea-Bissau">Economy of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-Bissau_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Guinea-Bissau's exports.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guinea-Bissau's <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita" class="mw-redirect">GDP per capita</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">lowest in the world</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">lowest on earth</a>. More than two-thirds of the population lives below the poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The economy depends mainly on agriculture; fish, <a href="/wiki/Cashew_nuts" title="Cashew nuts" class="mw-redirect">cashew nuts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ground_nuts" title="Ground nuts" class="mw-redirect">ground nuts</a> are its major exports.</p>
<p>A long period of political instability has resulted in depressed economic activity, deteriorating social conditions, and increased macroeconomic imbalances. It takes longer on average to register a new business in Guinea-Bissau (233 days or about 33 weeks) than in any other country in the world except <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>. [The Economist, Pocket World in Figures, 2008 Edition, London: Profile Books]</p>
<p>Guinea-Bissau has started to show some economic advances after a pact of stability was signed by the main political parties of the country, leading to an <a href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF" class="mw-redirect">IMF</a>-backed structural reform program.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The key challenges for the country in the period ahead are to achieve fiscal discipline, rebuild public administration, improve the economic climate for private investment, and promote economic diversification. After the country became independent from Portugal in 1974 due to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, the rapid exodus of the Portuguese civilian, military, and political authorities resulted in considerable damage to the country's economic infrastructure, <a href="/wiki/Social_order" title="Social order">social order</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a>.</p>
<p>After several years of economic downturn and political instability, in 1997, Guinea-Bissau entered the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a> monetary system, bringing about some internal monetary stability.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The civil war that took place in 1998 and 1999, and a military coup in September 2003 again disrupted economic activity, leaving a substantial part of the economic and social infrastructure in ruins and intensifying the already widespread poverty. Following the parliamentary elections in March 2004 and presidential elections in July 2005, the country is trying to recover from the long period of instability, despite a still-fragile political situation.</p>
<p>Beginning around 2005, drug traffickers based in Latin America began to use Guinea-Bissau, along with several neighboring West African nations, as a transshipment point to Europe for <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The nation was described by a United Nations official as being at risk for becoming a "<a href="/wiki/Narco-state" title="Narco-state" class="mw-redirect">narco-state</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-drugs_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drugs-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The government and the military have done little to stop drug trafficking, which increased after the 2012 coup d'état.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Guinea-Bissau is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Demographics of Guinea-Bissau">Demographics of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-Bissau_demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Guinea-Bissau_demography.png/350px-Guinea-Bissau_demography.png" width="350" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Guinea-Bissau_demography.png/525px-Guinea-Bissau_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Guinea-Bissau_demography.png/700px-Guinea-Bissau_demography.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="426" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-Bissau_demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guinea-Bissau's population between 1961 and 2003.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG/350px-Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG" width="350" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG/525px-Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG/700px-Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="625" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Guinee-Bissau.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guinea-Bissau's <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>, 2005. </div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabumainstreet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gabumainstreet.jpg/200px-Gabumainstreet.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gabumainstreet.jpg/300px-Gabumainstreet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gabumainstreet.jpg/400px-Gabumainstreet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabumainstreet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guinea-Bissau's third largest city, <a href="/wiki/Gab%C3%BA" title="Gabú">Gabú</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2010 revison of the UN <i>World Population Prospects</i>, Guinea-Bissau's population was 1,515,000 in 2010, compared to 518,000 in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The proportion of the population below the age of 15 in 2010 was 41.3%, 55.4% were aged between 15 and 65 years of age, while 3.3% were aged 65 years or older.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The population of Guinea-Bissau is ethnically diverse and has many distinct languages, customs, and social structures.</p>
<p>Guinea-Bissauans can be divided into the following ethnic groups:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka</a>-speaking people, who comprise the largest portion of the population and are concentrated in the north and northeast;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Balanta" title="Balanta" class="mw-redirect">Balanta</a> and Papel people, who live in the southern coastal regions; and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manjaco" title="Manjaco" class="mw-redirect">Manjaco</a> and Mancanha, who occupy the central and northern coastal areas.</li>
</ul>
<p>Most of the remainder are <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestiços</a></i> of mixed <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and African descent, including a <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verdean</a> minority.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Portuguese natives comprise a very small percentage of Guinea-Bissauans. After Guinea-Bissau gained independence, most of the Portuguese nationals left the country. The country has a tiny <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> These include traders and merchants of mixed Portuguese and Chinese ancestry from <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, a former Asian <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> colony.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Languages of Guinea-Bissau">Languages of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>14% of the population speaks the official language of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, made the language of government and national communication during the colonial years. 44% speak <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole" class="mw-redirect">Kriol</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">Portuguese-based creole language</a>, which is effectively a national language of communication among groups. The remainder speak a variety of native African languages unique to ethnicities.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Most Portuguese and Mestiços speak one of the African languages and Kriol as second languages. French is also taught in schools because Guinea-Bissau is surrounded by French-speaking nations. Guinea-Bissau is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" title="Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">Francophonie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Religion in Guinea-Bissau">Religion in Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:200px; background: white;">

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bafata1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/300px-Bafata1.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/450px-Bafata1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/600px-Bafata1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bafata1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Men in Islamic garb, <a href="/wiki/Bafat%C3%A1" title="Bafatá">Bafatá</a>, Guinea-Bissau.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the 20th century, most Bissau-Guineans practiced some form of <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Animism</a>. In the early 21st century, many have adopted Islam, which is now practiced by 50% of the country's population. Most of Guinea-Bissau's Muslims are of the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> denomination with approximately 2% belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> sect.<sup id="cite_ref-pew_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Approximately 10% of the country's population belong to the Christian community, and 40% continue to hold <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">Indigenous</a> beliefs. These statistics can be misleading, however, as many residents practice syncretic forms of Islamic and Christian faiths, combining their practices with traditional African beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref-1_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref-1-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a> estimates there are fewer than 5 physicians per 100,000 persons in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> down from 12 per 100,000 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The prevalence of HIV-infection among the adult population is 1.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-notTwentyPercent_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notTwentyPercent-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> 20% of infected pregnant women <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drug#Prevention_of_mother-to-child-transmission_.28PMTCT.29" title="Antiretroviral drug" class="mw-redirect">receive anti retroviral coverage</a> to prevent transmission to newborns.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> kills more residents; 9% of the population have reported infection,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> It causes three times as many deaths as AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, fewer than half of children younger than five slept under <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_net" title="Mosquito net">antimalaria nets</a> or had access to <a href="/wiki/Antimalarial_drugs" title="Antimalarial drugs" class="mw-redirect">antimalarial drugs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>'s estimate of life expectancy for a child born in 2008 was 49 years and 47 years for a boy.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite lowering rates in surrounding countries, <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> rates were reported in November 2012 to be on the rise, with 1,500 cases reported and nine deaths. A 2008 cholera epidemic in Guinea-Bissau affected 14,222 people and killed 225.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality" class="mw-redirect">maternal mortality</a> rate per 100,000 births for Guinea Bissau was 1000. This compares with 804.3 in 2008 and 966 in 1990. The under 5 mortality rate, per 1,000 births, was 195 and the neonatal mortality as a percentage of under 5's mortality was 24. The number of midwives per 1,000 live births was 3; one out of eighteen <a href="/wiki/Pregnant_women" title="Pregnant women" class="mw-redirect">pregnant women</a> die as a result of pregnancy.<sup id="cite_ref-SOWMY_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOWMY-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a 2013 UNICEF report, 50% of women in Guinea Bissau had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, Guinea Bissau had the 7th highest maternal mortality rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Education in Guinea-Bissau">Education in Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>Education is compulsory from the age of 7 to 13.<sup id="cite_ref-dol.gov_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dol.gov-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The enrollment of boys is higher than that of girls.<sup id="cite_ref-dol.gov_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dol.gov-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, the gross primary enrollment rate was 53.5%, with higher enrollment ratio for males (67.7%) compared to females (40%).<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor" class="mw-redirect">Child labor</a> is very common.<sup id="cite_ref-dol.gov_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dol.gov-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate" class="mw-redirect">literacy rate</a> was estimated at 55.3% (68.9% male, and 42.1% female).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Guinea-Bissau has several secondary schools (general as well as technical) and a <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="List of universities in Guinea-Bissau">number of universities</a>, to which an institutionally autonomous Faculty of Law as well as a Faculty of Medicine<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> have been added.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg/300px-Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg" width="300" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg/450px-Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="353" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea-bissau-bissau-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carnival in Bissau.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Music of Guinea-Bissau">Music of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<p>The music of Guinea-Bissau is usually associated with the <a href="/wiki/Polyrhythm" title="Polyrhythm">polyrhythmic</a> <a href="/wiki/Gumbe" title="Gumbe">gumbe</a> <a href="/wiki/Musical_genre" title="Musical genre" class="mw-redirect">genre</a>, the country's primary musical export. However, civil unrest and other factors have combined over the years to keep gumbe, and other genres, out of mainstream audiences, even in generally syncretist African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabasa" title="Cabasa">calabash</a> is the primary <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instrument</a> of Guinea-Bissau,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> and is used in extremely swift and rhythmically complex <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a>. Lyrics are almost always in <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole" class="mw-redirect">Guinea-Bissau Creole</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a>, and are often humorous and topical, revolving around current events and controversies, especially AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The word <i>gumbe</i> is sometimes used generically, to refer to any music of the country, although it most specifically refers to a unique style that fuses about ten of the country's <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Music of Guinea-Bissau">Tina and tinga</a> are other popular genres, while extent folk traditions include ceremonial music used in funerals, <a href="/wiki/Initiation" title="Initiation">initiations</a> and other rituals, as well as <a href="/wiki/Balanta" title="Balanta" class="mw-redirect">Balanta</a> brosca and kussundé, <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinga</a> djambadon, and the kundere sound of the <a href="/wiki/Bissagos_Islands" title="Bissagos Islands">Bissagos Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Cuisine of Guinea-Bissau">Cuisine of Guinea-Bissau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shucking_oysters_(483016387).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg/200px-Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg/300px-Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg/400px-Shucking_oysters_%28483016387%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shucking_oysters_(483016387).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People eating oysters in the capital, Bissau.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rice is a staple in the diet of residents near the coast and millet a staple in the interior. Fish, shellfish, fruits and vegetables are commonly eaten along with <a href="/wiki/Cereal_grain" title="Cereal grain" class="mw-redirect">cereal grains</a>, milk, <a href="/wiki/Curd" title="Curd">curd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whey" title="Whey">whey</a>. The Portuguese encouraged <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanut</a> production. <a href="/wiki/Vigna_subterranea" title="Vigna subterranea">Vigna subterranea</a> (Bambara groundnut) and <a href="/wiki/Macrotyloma_geocarpum" title="Macrotyloma geocarpum">Macrotyloma geocarpum</a> (Hausa groundnut) are also grown. <a href="/wiki/Black-eyed_pea" title="Black-eyed pea">Black-eyed peas</a> are also part of the diet. <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">Palm oil</a> is harvested.</p>
<p>Common dishes include <a href="/wiki/Soup" title="Soup">soups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a>. Common ingredients include <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, onion, tomato and <a href="/wiki/Plantain" title="Plantain" class="mw-redirect">plantain</a>. Spices, peppers and chilis are used in cooking, including <a href="/wiki/Aframomum_melegueta" title="Aframomum melegueta">Aframomum melegueta</a> seeds (Guinea pepper).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Flora_Gomes" title="Flora Gomes">Flora Gomes</a> is an internationally renowned film director; his most famous film is <i>Nha Fala</i> (<a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>: <i>My Voice</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Gomes's <i><a href="/wiki/Mortu_Nega" title="Mortu Nega">Mortu Nega</a></i> (<i>Death Denied</i>) (1988)<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> was the first fiction film and the second feature film ever made in Guinea-Bissau. (The first feature film was <i>N’tturudu</i>, by director Umban u’Kest in 1987.) At <a href="/wiki/FESPACO" title="FESPACO" class="mw-redirect">FESPACO</a> 1989, <i>Mortu Nega</i> won the prestigious Oumarou Ganda Prize. <a href="/wiki/Mortu_Nega" title="Mortu Nega">Mortu Nega</a> is in Creole with English subtitles. In 1992, Gomes directed <i>Udju Azul di Yonta</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> which was screened in the <a href="/wiki/Un_Certain_Regard" title="Un Certain Regard">Un Certain Regard</a> section at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="1992 Cannes Film Festival">1992 Cannes Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-festival-cannes.com_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festival-cannes.com-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Gomes has also served on the boards of many Africa-centric film festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-Ref-1-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Ref-1_49-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Ref-1_49-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/pu.html">"Guinea-Bissau"</a>, <i>CIA the World Factbook</i>, Cia.gov. <li id="cite_note-EB-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-EB_50-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EB_50-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/248853/Guinea-Bissau/">"Guinea-Bissau"</a>, <i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-pew-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-pew_51-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.pewforum.org/uploadedFiles/Topics/Religious_Affiliation/Muslim/the-worlds-muslims-full-report.pdf">"The World's Muslims: Unity and Diversity"</a>. Pew Forum on Religious &amp; Public life. 9 August 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 June</span> 2014</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=The+World%27s+Muslims%3A+Unity+and+Diversity&amp;rft.date=9+August+2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.pewforum.org%2FuploadedFiles%2FTopics%2FReligious_Affiliation%2FMuslim%2Fthe-worlds-muslims-full-report.pdf&amp;rft.pub=Pew+Forum+on+Religious+%26+Public+life&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The WHO identified only 78 physicians in the entire Guinea-Bissau health workforce in 2009 data. (<span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Health workforce, infrastructure, essential medicines"</a> (PDF). 2010. p.&#160;118.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Health+workforce%2C+infrastructure%2C+essential+medicines&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=118&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>) And the World Bank estimates that Guinea-Bissau had <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.google.com/publicdata?ds=wb-wdi&amp;met=sp_pop_totl&amp;idim=country:GNB&amp;dl=en&amp;hl=en&amp;q=guinea-bissau+population">1,575,446 residents in 2008</a>. At the current rate of growth, 2009 population was expected to reach about 1.61 million people. Only 0.0048% are known to be medical doctors involved in patient care. The WHO estimate an average of about 20 per 100,000 across Africa, but reports a density per 10,000 population of <b>&lt;0.5</b> in its <i>Physicians data covering the period to 2009</i>. Guinea-Bissau has an unusually high ratio of nursing staff to doctors: including nurses and <a href="/wiki/Midwive" title="Midwive" class="mw-redirect">midwives</a>; there are 64 medical professionals per 100,000 Bissau-Guineans</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The WHO estimates that there were 188 physicians working in the entire country as of 2007 (<span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS09_Table6.pdf">"Health workforce, infrastructure, essential medicines"</a>. 2009. p.&#160;98.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Health+workforce%2C+infrastructure%2C+essential+medicines&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS09_Table6.pdf&amp;rft.pages=98&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>). And The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimates that Guinea-Bissau had 1,541,040 residents in 2007 (<span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.google.com/publicdata?ds=wb-wdi&amp;met=sp_pop_totl&amp;idim=country:GNB&amp;dl=en&amp;hl=en&amp;q=guinea-bissau+population">"Midyear estimates of the resident population"</a>. 2010.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Midyear+estimates+of+the+resident+population&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2Fpublicdata%3Fds%3Dwb-wdi%26met%3Dsp_pop_totl%26idim%3Dcountry%3AGNB%26dl%3Den%26hl%3Den%26q%3Dguinea-bissau%2Bpopulation&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>). So, about 0.0122% of the permanent population were known to be medical doctors involved in patient care, as of 2007.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-notTwentyPercent-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-notTwentyPercent_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The WHO estimates a 1.8% HIV-infection rate from 2007 data among 15- to 49-year old Bissau-Guineans – see statistics on page 65 of: <span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"2. Cause-specific mortality and morbidity"</a> (PDF). WHO. 2010.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=2.+Cause-specific+mortality+and+morbidity&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pub=WHO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>. (The section's introduction describes estimation methodology).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of 2008, only 20% of HIV-infected mothers or sufferers with advanced cases had anti-retroviral drug access, see: <span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Health service coverage"</a>. WHO. 2010. p.&#160;91.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Health+service+coverage&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=91&amp;rft.pub=WHO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>. Coverage in the general population is lower.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Selected infectious diseases"</a>. WHO. 2010. p.&#160;76<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">9 June</span> 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Selected+infectious+diseases&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=76&amp;rft.pub=WHO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span> – 148,542 reported cases in 2008.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-57">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the 2010 WHO report, the latest Malaria mortality rate per 100,000 Bissau-Guineans (180) is substantially greater than that for AIDS (65). (<span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Cause-specific mortality and morbidity"</a>. WHO. 2010. p.&#160;64<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">9 June</span> 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Cause-specific+mortality+and+morbidity&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=64&amp;rft.pub=WHO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>) Among children younger than 5, malaria is nine times more deadly (p. 65).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Global Health Indicators: 4. WHO. 2010. p.&#160;91.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Global+Health+Indicators%3A+4.+Health+service+coverage&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=91&amp;rft.pub=WHO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/whosis/whostat/EN_WHS10_Part2.pdf">"Global Health Indicators: Mortality and burden of disease"</a>. 2010. p.&#160;50.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGuinea-Bissau&amp;rft.btitle=Global+Health+Indicators%3A+Mortality+and+burden+of+disease&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fwhosis%2Fwhostat%2FEN_WHS10_Part2.pdf&amp;rft.pages=50&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>. <i>Healthy</i> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> at birth was 42.
